\u003ccode\u003elist\u003c/code\u003e, in the same order as the names appear in the DataFrame.\nNote: Refer \u003ca <h2 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-correctionsclarifications" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#correctionsclarifications"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Corrections/Clarifications</h2>

<h2 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-overview" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#overview"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Overview</h2>
<p dir="auto">We will be making predictions about census data for Wisconsin using
regression models. You'll need to extract data from four files to
construct DataFrames suitable for training during this project:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>counties.geojson</code> - population and boundaries of each county in Wisconsin</li>
<li><code>tracts.shp</code> - boundaries of each census tract (counties are subdivided into tracts)</li>
<li><code>counties_tracts.db</code> - details about housing units per tract</li>
<li><code>land.zip</code> - details about land use (farm, forest, developed, etc.)</li>
</ul>
<h2 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-submission" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#submission"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Submission</h2>
<p dir="auto">Do all your work in a single p6.ipynb notebook file, and hand it in
when you're done.</p>
<p dir="auto">To run the local tester on your own VM type from the command line</p>
<p dir="auto"><code>python3 tester.py p6.ipynb</code></p>
<h1 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-group-part-75" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#group-part-75"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Group Part (75%)</h1>
<p dir="auto">For this portion of the project, you may collaborate with your group
members in any way (even looking at working code).  You may also seek
help from 320 staff (mentors, TAs, instructor).  You <b>may not</b>
seek receive help from other 320 students (outside your group) or
anybody outside the course.</p>
<h2 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-part-1-predicting-population-using-area" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#part-1-predicting-population-using-area"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Part 1: Predicting Population using Area</h2>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q1-how-many-counties-are-in-wisconsin" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q1-how-many-counties-are-in-wisconsin"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q1: How many counties are in Wisconsin?</h3>
<p dir="auto">Read <code>counties.geojson</code> into a GeoDataFrame and use it to calculate the number of counties in Wisconsin.</p>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q2-what-is-the-population-of-each-county-in-wi" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q2-what-is-the-population-of-each-county-in-wi"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q2: What is the population of each county in WI?</h3>
<p dir="auto">Create a geopandas plot that has a legend using the population from
the <code>POP100</code> column.</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/msyamkumar/cs320-s23-projects/blob/main/p6/q2.png"><img src="/msyamkumar/cs320-s23-projects/raw/main/p6/q2.png" width="500" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">The US Census Bureau does some surveys that attempt to sample the
population and others (like the decennial one) that attempt to count
everybody.  "POP100" means this is there attempt to count 100% of the
population (no sampling).  Similarly, "HU100" is a 100% count of
housing units.</p>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-feature-1-arealand" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#feature-1-arealand"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Feature 1: <code>AREALAND</code></h3>
<p dir="auto">Let's add an <code>AREALAND</code> column to your GeoDataFrame of counties so
that we can try to predict population based on area.</p>
<p dir="auto">You can get the area from the <code>counties_tracts.db</code> database.  Open it using <a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/sqlite3.html" rel="nofollow">sqlite3</a> then use <a href="https://pandas.pydata.org/docs/reference/api/pandas.read_sql.html" rel="nofollow">read_sql</a> on the DB connection to execute a query.
A great first query for an unfamiliar DB is <code>pd.read_sql("""SELECT * FROM sqlite_master""", conn)</code>.  That will show you all the tables the DB has. Try running <code>pd.read_sql("""SELECT * FROM ????""", conn)</code> for each table name to see what all the tables look like.</p>
<p dir="auto">Use data from the database to add an <code>AREALAND</code> column to your
GeoDataFrame.  The order of rows in your GeoDataFrame should not
change as part of this operation.</p>
<p dir="auto">After you've added <code>AREALAND</code> to your GeoDataFrame, use
<code>train_test_split</code> from <code>sklearn</code> to split the rows into <code>train</code> and
<code>test</code> datasets.</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>by default, <code>train_test_split</code> randomly shuffles the data differently each time it runs.  Pass <code>random_state=250</code> as a parameter so that it shuffles the same way as it did for us (so that you get the answers the tester expects).</li>
<li>Pass <code>test_size=0.25</code> to make the test set be one quarter of the original data and the other three quarters remaining in the training set.</li>
</ul>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q3-what-are-the-counties-in-the-test-dataset" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q3-what-are-the-counties-in-the-test-dataset"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q3: What are the counties in the test dataset?</h3>
<p dir="auto">Answer with a list, in the same order as the names appear in the original DataFrame.</p>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q4-how-much-variance-in-the-pop100-can-a-linearregression-model-explain-based-only-on-arealand" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q4-how-much-variance-in-the-pop100-can-a-linearregression-model-explain-based-only-on-arealand"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q4: How much variance in the <code>POP100</code> can a <code>LinearRegression</code> model explain based only on <code>AREALAND</code>?</h3>
<p dir="auto"><code>fit</code> the model to your <code>train</code> dataset and <code>score</code> it on your <code>test</code> dataset.</p>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q5-what-is-the-predicted-population-of-a-county-with-400-square-miles-of-area-according-to-the-model" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q5-what-is-the-predicted-population-of-a-county-with-400-square-miles-of-area-according-to-the-model"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q5: What is the predicted population of a county with 400 square miles of area, according to the model?</h3>
<p dir="auto">Consult the <a href="https://tigerweb.geo.census.gov/tigerwebmain/TIGERweb_attribute_glossary.html" rel="nofollow">Census documentation</a> to learn what units the data is in, and do any conversions necessary to answer the question.  Assume there are exactly 2.59 square kilometers per square mile for the purposes of your calculation.</p>
<h2 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-part-2-predicting-population-using-housing-units" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#part-2-predicting-population-using-housing-units"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Part 2: Predicting Population using Housing Units</h2>

<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-feature-2-hu100-housing-units" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#feature-2-hu100-housing-units"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Feature 2: <code>HU100</code> (housing units)</h3>
<p dir="auto">Look at the <code>tracts</code> table inside <code>counties_tracts.db</code> and find the
<code>HU100</code> column. Add a <code>HU100</code> column to your GeoDataFrame of counties,
similar to how you added <code>AREALAND</code>.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>The query to get housing units per county is more complicated than the
one for AREALAND</strong>.  County names are in the <code>counties</code> table and
<code>HU100</code> values are in the <code>tracts</code> table.  Fortunately, both tables
have a <code>COUNTY</code> column you can use to combine. Make sure to get the
total number of housing units for each county from the <code>tracts</code> table
by summing the housing units in each tract of the county.</p>
<p dir="auto">Split your updated GeoDataFrame into a train and test set, the same
way you did previously.</p>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q6-what-are-the-counties-in-the-test-dataset" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q6-what-are-the-counties-in-the-test-dataset"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q6: What are the counties in the test dataset?</h3>

<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q8-how-much-variance-in-the-pop100-can-a-linearregression-model-explain-based-only-on-hu100" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q8-how-much-variance-in-the-pop100-can-a-linearregression-model-explain-based-only-on-hu100"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q8: How much variance in the <code>POP100</code> can a <code>LinearRegression</code> model explain based only on <code>HU100</code>?</h3>
<p dir="auto">Answer with the average of 5 scores <a href="https://scikit-learn.org/stable/modules/generated/sklearn.model_selection.cross_val_score.html" rel="nofollow">produced by <code>cross_val_score</code> on the training data</a>.</p>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q9-what-is-the-standard-deviation-of-the-cross-validation-scores-from-q8" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q9-what-is-the-standard-deviation-of-the-cross-validation-scores-from-q8"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q9: What is the standard deviation of the cross validation scores from Q8?</h3>
<p dir="auto">Refrain from using statistics.stdev to calculate standard deviation. Variance is the average squared deviations from the mean, while standard deviation is the square root of this number.</p>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q10-what-is-the-formula-relating-pop100-and-hu100" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q10-what-is-the-formula-relating-pop100-and-hu100"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q10: What is the formula relating POP100 and HU100?</h3>
<p dir="auto">Fit your model to the training dataset to find the answer. Round the coefficient and intercept to 2 decimal places. Format the answer according to the following formula:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="POP100 = ????*HU100 + ????"><pre class="notranslate"><code>POP100 = ????*HU100 + ????
</code></pre></div>

<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q13-how-does-brown-county-look" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q13-how-does-brown-county-look"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q13: How does Brown County look?</h3>
<p dir="auto">NOTE: in lab, you had to use TIGERweb to get the geodata.  You
shouldn't do that here because we already did that saved the results
to <code>counties.geojson</code>, which you should use.  Otherwise, this is very
similar to the lab exercise.</p>
<p dir="auto">You can show the image like this:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="fig, ax = plt.subplots(figsize=(6,6))
ax.imshow(????, vmin=0, vmax=255)"><pre><span class="pl-s1">fig</span>, <span class="pl-s1">ax</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">plt</span>.<span class="pl-en">subplots</span>(<span class="pl-s1">figsize</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span>(<span class="pl-c1">6</span>,<span class="pl-c1">6</span>))

<p dir="auto">You can get the matrix for Brown County using <code>rasterio</code> and using the geometry in the DataFrame from <code>counties.geojson</code>.</p>
<p dir="auto">You can also define a custom color map (<a href="https://www.mrlc.gov/data/legends/national-land-cover-database-2019-nlcd2019-legend" rel="nofollow">corresponding to the legend</a> and pass <code>cmap=custom_cmap</code> to <code>imshow</code> to use it.</p>
<p dir="auto">You can create a custom color map using <code>ListedColormap</code>, which lets you specify red, green and blue (RGB) mixes for different values.  Here's an example for the land use data:</p>

<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q14-what-portion-of-brown-county-is-open-water" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q14-what-portion-of-brown-county-is-open-water"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q14: What portion of Brown County is "Open Water"?</h3>
<p dir="auto">Be careful!  Not everything in the matrix is Brown County -- be
sure not to count the cells with value 0.</p>
<p dir="auto">You can lookup the numeric code for "Open Water" and other types here: <a href="https://www.mrlc.gov/data/legends/national-land-cover-database-2019-nlcd2019-legend" rel="nofollow">https://www.mrlc.gov/data/legends/national-land-cover-database-2019-nlcd2019-legend</a></p>
<p dir="auto">Or, for your convenience, we typed the info from that page into a Python dictionary:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="land_use = {&quot;open_water&quot;: 11,

            <span class="pl-s">"woody_wetlands"</span>: <span class="pl-c1">90</span>,
            <span class="pl-s">"herbacious_wetlands"</span>: <span class="pl-c1">95</span>}</pre></div>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q15-what-is-the-relationship-between-pop100-and-________________" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q15-what-is-the-relationship-between-pop100-and-________________"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q15: What is the Relationship Between POP100 and ________________?</h3>

<h1 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-individual-part-25" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#individual-part-25"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Individual Part (25%)</h1>
<p dir="auto">You have to do the remainder of this project on your own.  Do not
discuss with anybody except 320 staff (mentors, TAs, instructor).</p>
<p dir="auto">For this part, you'll try to predict population on a <strong>per-census
tract</strong> basis (in contrast to our preceding per-county analysis),
using features calculated from the land use data.</p>
<h2 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-part-1" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#part-1"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Part 1:</h2>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>start with a GeoDataFrame dataset loaded from <code>tracts.shp</code></li>
<li>add feature columns to that dataset for every key in land_use(found under q14), with the column value being the number of units present of that land type, based on raster data from <code>lands.zip</code>.
Note : Computation takes considerable amount of time with raster data so try to minimize masking operations</li>
<li>split your GeoDataFrame into train/test using <code>random_state=200</code> and <code>test_size=0.20</code>.</li>
<li>Construct a regression model to predict POP100. Use all of the new columns you created in step 2 as the features for training.</li>
<li>Write a comment discussing what the graph is showing you and how you might use that information in building your own model(Part 2).</li>
</ol>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q16-what-features-does-your-model-rely-on-most" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q16-what-features-does-your-model-rely-on-most"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q16: What features does your model rely on most?</h3>
<p dir="auto">Answer with a bar plot showing feature and coefficent of feature in our trained model.</p>
<p dir="auto">Include a comment discussing what the graph is showing you and what it means for our model.</p>
<p dir="auto">You can search for "How can we interpret what features the model is relying on?" in the lecture examples:</p>
<p dir="auto"><a href="https://github.com/msyamkumar/cs320-lecture-notes/blob/main/lec_30_Regression_1/lecture.ipynb">https://github.com/msyamkumar/cs320-lecture-notes/blob/main/lec_30_Regression_1/lecture.ipynb</a></p>
<p dir="auto">In terms of tester scores, this question is weighted to be worth 2 regular questions.</p>
<h2 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-part-2" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#part-2"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Part 2:</h2>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>Construct at least 2 regression models predicting POP100. They should differ in terms of (a) what columns they use and/or (b) whether or not they're preceded by transformers in an sklearn Pipeline</li>
<li>Perform cross validation on both your models over your training dataset</li>
<li>Write a comment recommending which model you recommend for this prediction task. Factors you might consider are (a) mean of cross validation scores is high, (b) variance of cross validation scores is low, (c) model is simple, and (d) anything else you think is important.</li>
<li>Fit your recommended model to the entire training dataset and score it against the test dataset</li>
</ol>
<h3 tabindex="-1" dir="auto"><a id="user-content-q17-how-does-your-recommended-model-score-against-the-test-dataset" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" tabindex="-1" href="#q17-how-does-your-recommended-model-score-against-the-test-dataset"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a>Q17: How does your recommended model score against the test dataset?</h3>
<p dir="auto">This is just the number from step 4 above.  This cell is also a good
place to have your comment from step 3 (or there will be a manual
deduction).</p>
<p dir="auto">This question is weighted to be worth 3 regular questions.<br>
Your model needs to achieve explained variance higher than 0.35.</p>
